  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2bba46c8-f51c-4859-bb18-2e0a3209204f'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer856580033962646208"><b>Ten years ago, four people were brutally murdered. One girl lived.</b> <br/> <br/>No one believes her story. <br/>The police think she’s crazy. <br/>Her therapist thinks she’s suicidal. <br/>Everyone else thinks she’s a dangerous drunk. <br/>They’re all right—but did she see the killer? <br/> <br/>As the anniversary of the murders approaches, Faith Winters is released from the psychiatric hospital and yanked back to</span>
  <span id="freeText856580033962646208" style="display:none"><b>Ten years ago, four people were brutally murdered. One girl lived.</b> <br /> <br />No one believes her story. <br />The police think she’s crazy. <br />Her therapist thinks she’s suicidal. <br />Everyone else thinks she’s a dangerous drunk. <br />They’re all right—but did she see the killer? <br /> <br />As the anniversary of the murders approaches, Faith Winters is released from the psychiatric hospital and yanked back to the last spot on earth she wants to be—her hometown where the slayings took place. Wracked by the lingering echoes of survivor’s guilt, Faith spirals into a black hole of alcoholism and wanton self-destruction. Finding no solace at the bottom of a bottle, Faith decides to track down her sister’s killer—and then discovers that she’s the one being hunted. <br /> <br /><b>How can one woman uncover the truth when everyone’s a suspect—including herself?</b> <br /> <br />From the mind of Wall Street Journal bestselling author Christopher Greyson comes a story with twists and turns that take the reader on a journey of light and dark, good and evil, to the edge of madness. <i>The Girl Who Lived</i> should come with a warning label: Once you start reading, you won’t be able to stop. Not since <i>Girl on the Train</i> and <i>Gone Girl</i> has a psychological thriller kept readers so addicted—and guessing right until the last page. <br /> <br /></span>

<div class='spoiler'>
This question contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a href="/questions/1230980-christopher-greyson-did-you-attend-even"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Christopher Greyson. Did you attend even ONE AA meeting prior to writing this book? I'm sick to death of the way recovery meetings are portrayed in books. I'm only halfway through the book and have found so many inaccuracies I'm angry. We staunchly guard and practice anonymity. We don't judge when someone got to a meeting as to signing their paper. Too many more to list... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></a>
</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2694023405" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2694023405" />
    <a title="Misty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4348181-misty"><img alt="Misty" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542045550p2/4348181.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2694023405?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Misty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Misty" href="/user/show/4348181-misty">Misty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36678318-the-girl-who-lived">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4348181-misty?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2694023405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer925989425287470533">I think I need my “inner-rater” recalibrated. Many of the works I’m reading seem so majorly flawed, and yet the majority of readers appear to find them enjoyable and perfectly worthy of all the stars. <i>The Girl Who Lived</i> follows in that vein—an average mystery with a ridiculous ending and four and five star ratings that have left me shaking my head.<br/><br/>The plot is unique—to that I will concede. Faith is a twenty-two year old woman who has spent the past ten years in and out of mental hospitals after </span>
  <span id="freeText925989425287470533" style="display:none">I think I need my “inner-rater” recalibrated. Many of the works I’m reading seem so majorly flawed, and yet the majority of readers appear to find them enjoyable and perfectly worthy of all the stars. <i>The Girl Who Lived</i> follows in that vein—an average mystery with a ridiculous ending and four and five star ratings that have left me shaking my head.<br /><br />The plot is unique—to that I will concede. Faith is a twenty-two year old woman who has spent the past ten years in and out of mental hospitals after surviving a vicious attack that killed her best friend, her best friend’s mother, her own father and sister. Though local authorities have closed the case, convinced her father killed them all and then himself, Faith remembers another man—a man with the face of a rat—whom she believes committed all of the murders and then chased her into the woods. Now that she is finally out of the hospital (again) and in her own apartment, trying to tamp her rage and alcohol addiction, Rat Face is back—and he is stalking her. Is it Faith’s own fear manifesting as paranoia, or is the past finally catching up? That is the question that propels the rest of this book.<br /><br />So not only is the plot reasonably unique, the writing is also solid. The tone in each scene is well-developed, the dialogue is believable and Faith’s character is intriguing and complex. So why three stars? It’s difficult without spoilers, but suffice it to say that for me, the end is cheap and cliche and feels like a betrayal of the trust between author and reader. <br /><br />This would have been a four star read had I not had such a visceral reaction to the conclusion. As it stands, however, three stars feels generous.</span>
  <a data-text-id="925989425287470533" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Joey R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11232712-joey-r"><img alt="Joey R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528158785p2/11232712.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3282243927?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joey R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joey R." href="/user/show/11232712-joey-r">Joey R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36678318-the-girl-who-lived">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3282243927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14831670284240046906">4.5 stars— After reading “The Girl Who Lived” by Christoper Greyson I have one question... Why haven’t I heard of Christopher Greyson before now and why isn’t he a best selling author? This is the reason I subscribed to Kindle Unlimited is to find lesser known authors who write great books. That is how I found John Marrs, who is still one of my favorites. “The Girl Who Lived” is a very well written thriller that tells the story of Faith, the lone survivor of a brutal multiple killing. The author</span>
  <span id="freeText14831670284240046906" style="display:none">4.5 stars— After reading “The Girl Who Lived” by Christoper Greyson I have one question... Why haven’t I heard of Christopher Greyson before now and why isn’t he a best selling author? This is the reason I subscribed to Kindle Unlimited is to find lesser known authors who write great books. That is how I found John Marrs, who is still one of my favorites. “The Girl Who Lived” is a very well written thriller that tells the story of Faith, the lone survivor of a brutal multiple killing. The authorities have closed the case despite Faith claiming she saw a murderer she nicknamed “Ratface” kill her sister as they approached the trailer where the horrible events took place. Local law enforcement closed the case as a triple murder-suicide with Faith’s father being the killer. This leads to many problems for Faith and she ends up being institutionalized. The story begins as Faith leaves this mental institution and returns home as an adult with this mystery still unsolved. Greyson writes from Faith’s perspective and does an outstanding job getting into the mind of a tortured survivor and how she both copes with and attempts to solve the murders of several family members. The book interjects some great suspects ( from law enforcement to relatives) and really gives the reader the view that everyone is a suspect. The result is a very fast paced, enjoyable mystery that I couldn’t put down. I really enjoyed Faith’s reaction to what was happening around her and how she didn’t trust anyone instead of the usual character you get in these types of novels where you scratch your head asking how they could be so stupid. The book is good from start to finish and never loses its break-neck pace. I strongly recommend this book, and end with the note that if Christopher Greyson’s other novels are this good, I know what I will be doing for the next few months. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14831670284240046906" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2779898935310731909" style="display:none">She was just a child, but the nightmare she witnessed and survived was the end of the innocence of Faith Winters and only the beginning of ten years of living hell. Dark, mysterious and edgy, <b>THE GIRL WHO LIVED</b> by Christopher Greyson is a tale of guilt, deceit and borderline insanity for Faith, because as if surviving the deaths of her father, sister, best friend and best friend’s mother wasn’t horrific enough for a young teen, having her own mother profit at her expense and new found infamy could drive anyone to the edge. Ten years of institutions, doctors and drowning herself in alcohol to numb the pain, wouldn’t help, either. Faith knew she had to find who killed her family, if only to prove to herself that it wasn’t her. <br><br>It was when she moved back to her childhood town that she started seeing the Ratman, the man she saw all those years ago, the man she hid from under a log for four hours, the man no one believes exists. Hallucinations? Drunken illusions? Who can Faith trust? Who will believe in her? So far, she is alone, so far only the FBI agent says she will help, but she never does…leaving Faith lost in the vortex of the terror that resides in her mind, of the truth she knows is out there, if only someone would have her back…if only they would see her as more than <b>THE GIRL WHO LIVED</b>.<br><br>Christopher Greyson’s dark journey runs at breakneck speeds, so hang on for those sharp turns and beware of those who haunt the shadows, because people are dying and things are happening and they all point back to Faith and Faith has nowhere to hide when the secrets all around her start closing in...<br><br>I had to do a balancing act on the edge of my seat for this one! Wickedly twisted, terrifyingly dark, like running through a monster-filled maze alone, when the lights go out and that next turn is a dead end. Christopher Greyson has just made my “Authors to read when I want to be up all night,” list!<br><br>I received an ARC edition from Greyson Media.   <i>Reading The Girl Who Lived</i>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2171260320?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2171260320" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7409872568438292289">My first encounter with this author came via <i>Jack of Hearts</i>, a recent entry in his series featuring detective Jack Stratton. That one made a favorable impression - I look forward to the next one, hint, hint - and when I ran across this new standalone, I considered giving it a try. When I read the description, I was convinced that reading it would be a good idea - so even though it was just days before the release date, I requested, and was approved for, an advance copy (thank you).<br/><br/>In fact, it tu</span>
  <span id="freeText7409872568438292289" style="display:none">My first encounter with this author came via <i>Jack of Hearts</i>, a recent entry in his series featuring detective Jack Stratton. That one made a favorable impression - I look forward to the next one, hint, hint - and when I ran across this new standalone, I considered giving it a try. When I read the description, I was convinced that reading it would be a good idea - so even though it was just days before the release date, I requested, and was approved for, an advance copy (thank you).<br /><br />In fact, it turned out to be a <i>great</i> idea; my concern that I might not get it finished on time vanished after a handful of chapters. NFL and college football games came and went unwatched, Lawrence Welk got recorded, and I even skipped at least one lunch because I couldn't bring myself to put it down. A 5-star rating? A no-brainer.<br /><br />The book's title reflects the title of another book - one written by the mother of Faith Winters. Ten years earlier, Faith's beloved sister Kim and two others died violent deaths, reportedly at the hand of her father, who then committed suicide. Faith, who was present at the time, managed to hide out in the dark woods. She escaped certain death, yes, but she was left with deep psychological wounds. Faith's mother, a therapist, worked through her own grief by way of writing a tell-all book about the daughter - Faith - who survived.<br /><br />Faith continued to bury her anguish by way of alcohol, temper tantrums and other behavioral no-nos, which in turn landed her in a psychiatric hospital. But now, close to the anniversary of the murders, she gets the okay for release - on the condition that she return to the hometown in which all the blood was shed and participate in group therapy programs. No matter what she tries, though, she's not able to shake off the trauma of her past - nor her belief that the father she loved did not commit the awful crimes. That's because she'd seen another person at the scene back then - an unknown man she calls "Rat Face."<br /><br />But alas, no one - not even the police - believed her then, nor do they believe her now. Even when she spots him once again, everyone thinks it's all in her twisted mind. Everyone, that is, except Rat Face, who learns that Faith has spotted him again. Now, he - and possibly his partners in crime - must do whatever it takes to keep from being identified, including making sure that this time, they leave no witnesses. Several twists and turns lead to an exciting conclusion (I won't say it's totally satisfying, but the loose ends get pretty well tied up). In short? Very well done and highly recommended.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7409872568438292289" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3293207687" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3293207687" />
    <a title="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24156068-christina---recipe-a-read"><img alt="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580849831p2/24156068.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3293207687?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" href="/user/show/24156068-christina---recipe-a-read">Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36678318-the-girl-who-lived">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3293207687" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10525755683249796956"><b>5, brilliantly crafted with a surprisingly emotional ending stars!!</b><br/><br/>Ah yes, the elusive 5th star in the mystery/thriller genre rating system. At least for me, when you read so many thrillers back to back it's pretty easy to see the formula for writing. That's certainly not to say that I myself could do that, I definitely can not. My only point is, at a certain point it becomes par for the course instead of really taking you by surprise. So when something new, something rich and exciting comes alo</span>
  <span id="freeText10525755683249796956" style="display:none"><b>5, brilliantly crafted with a surprisingly emotional ending stars!!</b><br /><br />Ah yes, the elusive 5th star in the mystery/thriller genre rating system. At least for me, when you read so many thrillers back to back it's pretty easy to see the formula for writing. That's certainly not to say that I myself could do that, I definitely can not. My only point is, at a certain point it becomes par for the course instead of really taking you by surprise. So when something new, something rich and exciting comes along it makes it even more fun. That's the case with <i>The Girl Who Lived</i>. <br /><br />Who is the girl who lived? Her name is Faith Winters and she bore witness to the brutal slaying of her sister, best friend, her best friends mother and her beloved father on her 13th birthday. Barely surviving the encounter herself Faith spirals into a pit of depression, alcoholism and unrelenting anguish. After local police close the case coming to a conclusion that Faith knows is wrong, her survivors guilt leads her down a path that eventually leads to her incarceration. <br /><br /><b>Like paper clips to a magnet, they were drawn back to the same spot, helpless in the grip of instinct, unable to go in any other direction.</b><br /><br />Upon Faiths release from prison, she's forced to return to the one place that has haunted her for a decade - her home town. As she works to try once again to dig herself out of the grave through court mandated AA meetings, survivors groups and "family" time with her mother, her past comes back to haunt her. Faith doesn't remember the whole truth, but she knows without a shadow of a doubt that what the police say happened is wrong. When she sees a man she's deems "Rat Face" who she remember from the night of the slayings in town, it sends her into a frenzy to uncover the truth about her loved ones murders - no matter what the cost. <br /><br /><b>Hush, little girl, rest your head. Hush, little girl, stay in bed. The sun and your friends are fast asleep. Now’s not a time to cry and weep. For in your dreams, there we’ll be. Hurry now, and follow me.</b><br /><br />Wowewow could I not put this book down. I read it in one sitting and couldn't tear my eyes away from the pages as the words played out in my head like a movie. Greyson did such a phenomenal job threading the needle of the unreliable narrator trope while simultaneously creating a character in Faith that you couldn't help but root for. From the start your heart breaks and bleeds for Faith's story and what she has endured from such a young age but you can't help but want to shake her out of her self-induced stooper. While Faith's character had the most dimension and the most layers to her personality and her story, each character brought with them their own perspectives and view on a true tragedy and added a continued depth to the story that kept me questioning from page one. <br /><br />As I've mentioned before, it can't be said that it's difficult to "pull one over" on me because despite the fact that I spend the entire book questioning everything, I'm still generally wrong. There's the excitement of being genuinely surprised by a books final twists - and boy does this book have them in spades. Then there's the delight in being surprised by the level of depth that a story has once you finish it. For me, the true meaning of a story can't be fully realized until you've seen how an author chooses to <i>end</i> it. It's always seemed so much harder to end a story than to start it so I'm always tickled when an author knocks it out of the park, and <i>The Girl Who Lived</i> did the damn thing. There's so much emotion in Faith's story, so much sadness and pain in her life that I think the book would've been remiss to ignore in the ending. I found myself a soft blubbering mess when I got to the last chapter of the book and Greyson did an incredible job of not only tying up all loose ends, but truly giving Faith's story the grace it deserved. <br /><br /><b>Her father called her Spitfire.</b><br /><br />If you can't tell already, I loved it. If you're a fan of mystery/thriller novels and you're looking for one to shake things up, that breaks up the formulaic monotony the genre can sometimes fall into, this is the book for you. The emotional depth of not just the story, but it's individual characters had me teetering on the edge of my seat as I raced to finish this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10525755683249796956" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2729305162" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2729305162" />
    <a title="Shelby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45436992-shelby"><img alt="Shelby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578351688p2/45436992.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2729305162?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelby" href="/user/show/45436992-shelby">Shelby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45436992-shelby?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2729305162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11405839895123132657">Bleh.<br/><br/>So I had a lot of issues with this story--well, let me rephrase. There were a lot of things about this story that I didn't like. <br/><br/>Let's start with the main character. Personally...and I guess I should stress the <i>personally</i> part of this because this is completely, 100% my opinion and I'm sure there are people out there who would disagree, but...Faith's character just never did much for me. She was too disoriented? I guess would be the best word? She never really seemed capable of stopping to </span>
  <span id="freeText11405839895123132657" style="display:none">Bleh.<br /><br />So I had a lot of issues with this story--well, let me rephrase. There were a lot of things about this story that I didn't like. <br /><br />Let's start with the main character. Personally...and I guess I should stress the <i>personally</i> part of this because this is completely, 100% my opinion and I'm sure there are people out there who would disagree, but...Faith's character just never did much for me. She was too disoriented? I guess would be the best word? She never really seemed capable of stopping to think, even for a second, and because of that, she spends 90% of the story running this way and that way, drinking, and making decisions that are (at least to me) like the worst possible, stupidest, most impulsive decisions possible. It's hard to feel any sort of connection with her because she doesn't allow herself to connect to anyone and it's hard to root for her when she spends the entire book actively working against herself. I mean... On the one hand, yes, addiction is real and hard to beat, and tragedy/trauma leave their own unique scars on people and affect them differently, but...you just got out of a mental institution that you hated (and spent an entire year plotting on how to get out of) and your only stipulations of your freedom are to attend some AA/Survivor's meetings and not to drink...and the first night you're free (after being sober for a whole year) you go...take six shots at a bar? There didn't seem to be any "Oh no maybe I shouldn't do this" thought about it or struggle against it, either. And throughout the rest of the book, her actions reflect that sort of thought process (well, the lack thereof). <br /><br />And then, thoughout the novel, it sort of felt like a pop up book--I'm trying to think of a pop culture example to compare it to, but basically, especially at the end of the novel, these characters were just popping up in every corner of the room like a soap opera "Don't trust him!" Then "he" enters the room: "No, don't trust <i>him</i>!" And then a third--"Don't trust either of them!" and so on and so forth. <br /><br />The ending was a really big disappointment to me, essentially. Was it surprising? Yes. But it didn't...make sense to me. I don't think the antagonist's motivations were strong enough, and I don't think there was enough foreshadowing/build-up throughout the beginning of the novel for the ending to fit for me.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />UGH Let me just start with the biggest spoiler of all-- the MOM is the killer?? For money and to be with...Thad??<br /><br />Look, okay, I get it, if she arranged for the dad to be killed--I mean, maybe...well, actually no. I don't get it.<br /><br />Here's a big issue I've seen in a lot of books I've read, and it's something authors should always ask themselves--Why not? This is a question that needs to be asked in terms of motives and the ways characters go about getting the things they want. In this context, if Perf Psychologist Mom wanted to have her fantasy life with dad...Why not just divorce him? I would think, in the 21st century, it wouldn't ruin her image (unless she was a Republican running for office with the "sanctity of marriage" platform, maybe??), and since her "perfect" child Kim was old enough to be in college, there wouldn't be any custody issues--she could just surrender full custody of Faith to the father. And then, bingo! Marry Thad, invite Kim over every weeknight and fawn over her perfect new fiancé Tommy, and then just pretend the ex-husband and Faith don't exist. <br /><br />My point is, if there's an easier way for things to be accomplished, why wouldn't a character take it? I mean, I recognize that <i>all</i> of the mom's "problems" might not be solved via divorce, but a good 99% of them would be, and they would come without all the issues that HIRING A COUPLE OF MURDERERS do. Her blasé attitude about the other mom/daughter deaths didn't make any sense, and she never even mentioned that her murder-for-hire plan killed an entire third of her "Dream life" by killing Kim, too. The only reason the murder case was originally shut in the first place was because they assumed the dad killed the family (on really, really weak evidence, btw) and that wasn't part of the original murder-for-hire plan. Why didn't she cultivate a motive (AKA ask the perps to make it look like a robbery gone wrong, ask them to purposely frame the dad by shooting--not stabbing--everyone, etc etc?)<br /><br />The OG murder-plot doesn't really make sense to me, and neither does the second half. Could the mother make more money via a sequel memoir of her daughter's freedom/relapse? Yes. Wouldn't it be easier, though, for the mom to just get power of attorney over her crazy, dangerous daughter (a relatively easy thing to do, I imagine, considering her history of mental illness/suicide attempts?/violence/drinking, her ignorance of the legal system/the way things work in the "real" world, and her lack of resources to fight back against the legal system??)<br /><br />If the mom had gotten power of attorney, she could have easily gotten her daughter committed to an institution/rehab center/long-term care facility for her daughter's own "health and safety." And then...boom. No more daughter-who-saw-the-killer-and-never-believed-her-father-did-it issues, no daughter talking about those issues to anyone (including the mom's therapist partner), nothing. And then the mom could continue living her life with Thad, making money off of the first book--with the anniversary coming up, it would still sell more copies and make plenty of money--and the mom's life would be as un-threatened and idyllic as it had been for the ten years before that. It just doesn't make sense for her to jeopardize everything she's built in the last 10 years by letting her daughter be free and actively question the OG murders. If nothing else, she should have hired the same dudes to stage her daughter's murder/death/suicide or even killed her own daughter (since she doesn't seem to have any qualms about it!!!) by switching out the daughter's pills or something similar.<br /><br />The convoluted lengths the mom went to just to...marry Thad and gain <i>more</i> money off a sequel book (again, not enough motive when compared to the risks it posed to her "dream" life) just never worked for me.<br /><br />But let's move past that.<br /><br />I think--and this is an odd criticism for me--that there were almost...too many suspects. Or maybe it's just the way that they kept popping up, like I described earlier. It made it feel like it was Faith against the world--which maybe would have worked with a more capable/less disoriented protagonist, but...it never felt like Faith was up to the task of taking down/figuring out the real villain--and she wasn't! In the end, the only reason anything worked out for her was because the mom triggered her own downfall. It was entirely a stroke of her mother's bad luck (I'm hesitant to even say that it was Faith's good luck, honestly) that lead to Faith surviving the day and her mother being caught.<br /><br />ALSO! Why didn't the mom make it look like Faith had shot herself in the house with Hunter (or Cory or whatever his name was)? Then no one would be alive to question what had happened (well, the cameras, obvs, but the mom didn't know about those, so to her mind, you get the point). Wouldn't it have been easier than trying to make it look like Faith had killed Hunter/Cory/Red Camaro dude and then...hit herself in the head?<br /><br />And can we talk about that scene at the end with "Agent Henry"?? <br /><br />God, I'm so over "twist" endings where characters end up being figments of the protag's imagination or the book ends up being "just a dream." It was cool once, now it's cliché and tbh it feels lazy, can we move on??<br /><br />If that's not enough of a "reason" for me to dislike it, let me also poke some holes in it: Hallucinations are like dreams, in that they are built from pieces of your memory. Where the ever loving hell did Henryika Whatever-her-last-name-was come from?? Why would Faith imagine her, just her, in all these convenient moments when she was alone? (Hallucinations are rarely so convenient and polite). <br /><br />And, finally, what was the fucking point?? Seriously? What did Henry do for the plot/for Faith that justified her existence in the novel? Did she encourage Faith to stay sober? Yes, but did it actually have any effect on Faith's sobriety? NO--she went drinking the next day! Did she tell Faith to lay low and protect herself? Yes, but, again, did Faith listen to that? No. Did she act as a strengthening, helpful force that convinced Faith to stay alive? No, because even though she offered some compelling reasons for Faith to stay alive, Faith still wanted to commit suicide and would have done it if she hadn't been interrupted at the cabin (again, the DAY AFTER she had that convo with Henry!)<br /><br />And look, you can argue that Henry was like the ghost of her sister urging her to stay sober/alive whatever--but why not just do that?? Why not just have Faith imagine her sister there, guiding her? It would certainly make more sense for a drunk/heavily medicated woman to hallucinate her dead sister than it would for her to hallucinate a brash FBI agent. And at the end, Henry turned into Kim anyway, so what was the point?? It feels like a "Gotcha" moment for the readers--a character/plot point created solely to create a "twist" ending, because if Faith had been imagining Kim, we would have known that it wasn't real. (As an afterthought, imagine the added parallel/cool note of Faith "seeing" and "talking" to Kim and then meeting Mrs. Henderson, who talks to what Faith believes is Kim's ghost--instead of this "ooo, crazy knitting lady at a survivor's meeting" vibe, Faith could have believed that she found an actual ally and it would have strengthened her own belief that she was really hearing from Kim's ghost.)<br /><br />But instead, we get that tooth-achingly sweet (in a bad way, imo) and clichéd scene at the end where Henry magically turns into Kim's ghost, and the sisters have a touching and w/e goodbye scene. It was predictable, boring, and it's been done a thousand times. Give me something new.<br /><br />One question I'm left with: Did Hunter/Cory/Whatshisname actually kill other families/people? The idea that he was serial killer was given to us by Henry, which means that Faith technically made it up, but the book never directly addressed whether the "serial killer" thing was true or not. <br /><br />Also, as a last, parting criticism--I think Hunter/Cory/Whatshisname suffered as a villain because he was such a strawman. He wasn't fleshed out--he was just a shadow created and used by the author to hide the mom's involvement until the twist ending, which is not necessarily a bad thing, but his character suffered from it because he didn't have any depth, and so he became one of those "just a crazy, murder-loving psychopath" characters who we don't really know anything about besides the fact that they like killing people. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11405839895123132657" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2704228879887014537">Faith Winters and her sister, Kim, were going to their parents’ cabin to celebrate Faith’s 13th birthday.   <span id="freeText2704228879887014537" style="display:none">Faith Winters and her sister, Kim, were going to their parents’ cabin to celebrate Faith’s 13th birthday. It was going to be a very special day and Faith was excited. But when they arrived at the cabin, something didn’t seem right. As they approached, the door opened and someone grabbed Kim. Kim screamed for Faith to run……..<br /><br />Ten years had gone by and Faith had never fully recovered from the horror she experienced that day. Faith’s sister, father, best friend and her best friend’s mother were all found murdered. But now, after being treated in a psychiatric hospital, Faith is being released. But she is determined to seek justice for the victims, and to find the murderer.<br /><br />The Girl Who Lived is a first rate, fast paced psychological thriller that will keep you on the edge of your seat until the final pages! Twists and turns abound as you reach the final, unexpected conclusion. Thank you to author Christopher Greyson, Greyson Media LLC, and NetGalley for giving me the opportunity to read the ARC of this suspenseful book! <br /></span>

<div id="review_2289888238" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2289888238" />
    <a title="Lucy Banks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57486568-lucy-banks"><img alt="Lucy Banks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483536933p2/57486568.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2289888238?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy Banks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy Banks" href="/user/show/57486568-lucy-banks">Lucy Banks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2289888238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7790353335022706265"><i>I received a copy of this book from Netgalley, in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/><b>A real page-turner, good fun to read.</b><br/><br/>Generally speaking, I'm not a mad fan of the suspense / crime genre, but I'm always happy to give <i>any</i> book a try, especially if it's got some good reviews. <br/><br/>I commenced reading <i>The Girl Who Lived</i> with the expectation that it would comply with the standard genre formula, but offer a gripping, fast-paced read. It didn't disappoint. Yes, it was marginally formulaic, but I had a lot of</span>
  <span id="freeText7790353335022706265" style="display:none"><i>I received a copy of this book from Netgalley, in exchange for an honest review.</i><br /><br /><b>A real page-turner, good fun to read.</b><br /><br />Generally speaking, I'm not a mad fan of the suspense / crime genre, but I'm always happy to give <i>any</i> book a try, especially if it's got some good reviews. <br /><br />I commenced reading <i>The Girl Who Lived</i> with the expectation that it would comply with the standard genre formula, but offer a gripping, fast-paced read. It didn't disappoint. Yes, it was marginally formulaic, but I had a lot of fun reading it! <br /><br />It starts in an institution for people with severe mental health problems; and that's where we first meet Faith; a twenty-something year old girl with a seriously troubled past. It transpires that her sister and father were murdered in front of her, as was her friend and her mother. The only thing Faith remembers clearly is 'Rat Face', a nasty-looking, thin faced man who was there at the time.<br /><br />On her release, Faith swears to stay off the booze, and not go looking for revenge - both promises that she fails to keep. She starts to see Rat Face everywhere, and worse still, he's pursuing her...<br /><br />Let's start with what was good about this book. I liked Faith a lot. She's brittle, aggressive and completely unapologetic; and I like that the author didn't soften her up or dumb her down. Why should a protagonist have to be likeable, anyway? This made the trauma that she'd suffered feel far more authentic. <br /><br />It was a well-crafted, well-paced read too. At no point was I bored, and I kept those pages turning, keen to find out what was going to happen next. I also didn't guess the final ending, which is always a good thing. <br /><br />However, I had some minor issues with the final pages (and this is so often the problem for me, when reading books like this!). I found it very over-sensationalised and too twisty-turny to comprehend. In short, my disbelief can only be suspended so far, and with this book, it snapped quite a way before the end. <br /><br />There were a few other points where I felt this too - that certain scenarios just didn't feel credible. But I am fully prepared to admit that this is due to me questioning things too much, and other readers may be far happier to go along for the ride without over-thinking it all! <br /><br />To conclude? It's a good example of a book of this genre, done in an entertaining, engaging way. If you're in love with this style of book, it's definitely one to add to the list. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7790353335022706265" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Joint" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Joint" href="/user/show/19758811-sarah-joint">Sarah Joint</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2368072205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12968847371521444369"><b>This is remarkably fast-paced and a really easy read.</b> The case is undoubtedly intriguing, but for me the book suffered from some hard to believe situations and some really stilted dialogue. I'm certainly an outlier in those opinions, as it's gotten very high reviews on Good Reads. Three stars from me still means I enjoyed it, but not quite enough to give it a four. It does keep you guessing! <br/><br/>Ten years ago, Faith Winters ran and hid from an attacker. That's the only thing that saved her from suff</span>
  <span id="freeText12968847371521444369" style="display:none"><b>This is remarkably fast-paced and a really easy read.</b> The case is undoubtedly intriguing, but for me the book suffered from some hard to believe situations and some really stilted dialogue. I'm certainly an outlier in those opinions, as it's gotten very high reviews on Good Reads. Three stars from me still means I enjoyed it, but not quite enough to give it a four. It does keep you guessing! <br /><br />Ten years ago, Faith Winters ran and hid from an attacker. That's the only thing that saved her from suffering the same fate of four others: her older sister, her father, her best friend, and her best friend's mother.<b> In only one night, her life is destroyed and her family is cut in half, with only her mother and her remaining.</b> The killer has never been caught, and Faith has spent the years back and forth from mental hospitals. As the ten year anniversary approaches, she's released back into the town where it all began. <b>Still determined to find the killer but waylaid by her own fractured mind and addiction to alcohol, she finds herself in plenty of perilous situations. In her world, no one can be trusted and everyone is a suspect. But can she find the killer before she's found first... or locked back up? </b><br /><br />Recommended to fans of thrillers who don't mind some suspension of disbelief and lots of action. The ending is explosive.<br /><br /><i>I received a copy of this book from Net Galley and Greyson Media Associates, thank you! My review is honest and unbiased.</i></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3267764016" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3267764016" />
    <a title="Kimberly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41884037-kimberly"><img alt="Kimberly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561219567p2/41884037.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3267764016?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kimberly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kimberly" href="/user/show/41884037-kimberly">Kimberly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41884037-kimberly?shelf=amazon-prime-reads">amazon-prime-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41884037-kimberly?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41884037-kimberly?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3267764016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10733029592155222995">It's a deadly game of cat and mouse as Faith tracks down the man responsible for killing half her family. The action explodes from the pages from beginning to end. The twists kept me guessing and the reveal was surprising. I felt like the last chapter too an odd turn but I liked it anyway.<br/><br/>Over all, it was a good read but reader should be warned there is plenty of violence which is to be expected and there is quite a bit of talk about suicide.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

This book is about Faith, the lone survivor of a brutal murdering spree and her quest for justice. It depicts her battles with depression and mental illness as well. <div id="review_2173578000" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2173578000" />
    <a title="Peggy Jaeger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30426949-peggy-jaeger"><img alt="Peggy Jaeger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472239506p2/30426949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2173578000?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Peggy Jaeger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peggy Jaeger" href="/user/show/30426949-peggy-jaeger">Peggy Jaeger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2173578000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1241749498153495181">We all deal with grief in different ways. Some of us survive a tragedy and move on with our lives. Some of us do not.<br/><br/>Ten years ago, when she was 13, Faith Winters watched the brutal killing of 4 people she knew and loved. And for 10 years she’s been in and out of trouble with the law and committed to psychiatric institutions because of it. As the 10th anniversary of the murders approaches, she is released from her most recent psychiatric incarceration and sent back to a world where no one believ</span>
  <span id="freeText1241749498153495181" style="display:none">We all deal with grief in different ways. Some of us survive a tragedy and move on with our lives. Some of us do not.<br /><br />Ten years ago, when she was 13, Faith Winters watched the brutal killing of 4 people she knew and loved. And for 10 years she’s been in and out of trouble with the law and committed to psychiatric institutions because of it. As the 10th anniversary of the murders approaches, she is released from her most recent psychiatric incarceration and sent back to a world where no one believes anything she says. They see her as the sole victim who survived a massacre, never as her own person.<br /><br />Faith has always maintained that the man who was accused of the crime – her father – was innocent. No one believed her back then and no one does today.<br /> Faith’s goal now is to find the real killer.<br /><br />Thrown back into a world where she is an outcast, a felon, and considered delusional, Faith must weave and bob through court-ordered therapy sessions, parole meetings and a deal with a mother who profited in the worst possible way from the tragedy of the past.<br /><br />When we first meet Faith, I will admit, she was a totally unsympathetic character for me. The chip on her shoulder had to weigh 5oo pounds and her I hate the world mentality was off-putting. As the story progressed I grew less annoyed with her and began to see her more as a single-minded, multifaceted young woman who, even though the judicial and mental health systems had failed her, never the less stuck to her internal motivation of proving her father innocent at all costs – even her own life. The people surrounding her are all suspects, their behaviors, their words, even the way they treat her are untrustworthy and make Faith feel she is truly on her own – and she is.<br /><br />In this book, Faith survives one event after another that probably would have felled a lesser willed person. Even though she states frequently that she’d like nothing more than to die, her will to live and survive each event is strong.<br /><br />By the final chapters of the book, I was rooting for her to not only find the real killer but to finally believe life was worth living.<br /><br />I was given an arc of this novel from Netgalley for an honest opinion and I can truthfully say The Girl Who Lived is a thrilling rollercoaster ride of terror, harsh emotion, and redemption. Well worth the read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1241749498153495181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2170791358" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2170791358" />
    <a title="Sandy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5913149-sandy"><img alt="Sandy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588984701p2/5913149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2170791358?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandy" href="/user/show/5913149-sandy">Sandy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5913149-sandy?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5913149-sandy?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5913149-sandy?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2170791358" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13051833663883403731">She saw Rat Face man on Death Day and now she cannot get his face off her mind. Faith has spent almost ten years in mental institutes and today her mother is signing her out, she will finally be free, or will she? Faith is having a hard time with the rules of her probation, she needs the alcohol for the rough days and the gun for security and protection. She’d love to join the others but the need for vengeance is stronger. They saw each other by accident, Rat Face and Faith and what happens next</span>
  <span id="freeText13051833663883403731" style="display:none">She saw Rat Face man on Death Day and now she cannot get his face off her mind. Faith has spent almost ten years in mental institutes and today her mother is signing her out, she will finally be free, or will she? Faith is having a hard time with the rules of her probation, she needs the alcohol for the rough days and the gun for security and protection. She’d love to join the others but the need for vengeance is stronger. They saw each other by accident, Rat Face and Faith and what happens next is anyone’s guess but it seems as if the tables have been turned.<br /><br />There were a few instances where Faith’s behavior made me cringe, what was this girl thinking? She was stubborn and certain in her movements, she’s on a mission. She encounters plenty of roadblocks along the way but they don’t stop her, she finds ways around them. It’s an intense, thrilling novel with an incredible ending. <br /><br />I received a copy of this novel from NetGalley and Greyson Media in exchange for an honest review. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13051833663883403731" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2159246511" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2159246511" />
    <a title="Aimee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40384772-aimee"><img alt="Aimee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424211741p2/40384772.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2159246511?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aimee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aimee" href="/user/show/40384772-aimee">Aimee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40384772-aimee?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2159246511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9077486210552974143">I received an advanced copy of The Girl Who Lived.<br/><br/>I am a huge fan of the Jack Stratton Series, by Christopher Greyson, so I was excited to receive The Girl Who Lived. I like mystery, suspense, thrillers, and psychological thrillers in general. This book definitely fits into those categories.<br/><br/>Although the writing style is Christopher Greyson it is a departure from the Jack Stratton Series. The Girl Who Lived is a bit darker, it deals with survivors guilt and addictions that manifest themselves aft</span>
  <span id="freeText9077486210552974143" style="display:none">I received an advanced copy of The Girl Who Lived.<br /><br />I am a huge fan of the Jack Stratton Series, by Christopher Greyson, so I was excited to receive The Girl Who Lived. I like mystery, suspense, thrillers, and psychological thrillers in general. This book definitely fits into those categories.<br /><br />Although the writing style is Christopher Greyson it is a departure from the Jack Stratton Series. The Girl Who Lived is a bit darker, it deals with survivors guilt and addictions that manifest themselves after a horrendous crime and the aftermath. The main character, Faith, feels she is a broken person. She is alive, but not living. I think anyone reading this book that can relate to her anxiety, despair, and emptiness will appreciate her struggle. But you don't need to be a survivor to get wrapped up in the suspense.<br /><br />I was totally surprised by the ending. I didn't see it coming. But all of the puzzle pieces start to fall into place as you look back. <br /><br />I thought the first two chapters were a bit slow, but you really want to hang in there. I think those first few chapters explain where Faith is and why. Then the story starts picking up... and then I could not put down the book. I was reading from about 12:30am to 6:30am. I was going to read just until I fell asleep. But it is morning, I just finished the book, my eyes are dry and bloodshot and it is time to feed the dog breakfast.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9077486210552974143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer40641030256756196">What a fantastic roller coaster ride!<br/><br/>I was caught off guard, I laughed, and I cried. I wanna blame PMS, but you guys... this ending is powerful.<br/><br/><br/>I wanna be just like Faith, minus the tragedy she endures. This girl is the strongest woman I've ever encountered. When faced with a situation where you can literally trust no one, what would you do? Faith? Well she fought and fought hard. I want to hug her, and tell her I'm proud of her and I admire her.<br/><br/><br/>I don't even think I can put into words how much I</span>
  <span id="freeText40641030256756196" style="display:none">What a fantastic roller coaster ride!<br /><br />I was caught off guard, I laughed, and I cried. I wanna blame PMS, but you guys... this ending is powerful.<br /><br /><br />I wanna be just like Faith, minus the tragedy she endures. This girl is the strongest woman I've ever encountered. When faced with a situation where you can literally trust no one, what would you do? Faith? Well she fought and fought hard. I want to hug her, and tell her I'm proud of her and I admire her.<br /><br /><br />I don't even think I can put into words how much I loved this book. Suspicion is cast upon so many characters, and they all fit the bill. But the reality of the thing is so much crazier than anyone could anticipate! <br /><br />I'd never say this in real life, but thank god for hidden cameras :) </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7N5/xPIZFXm4YYJNdRtTK1PpYCLIjItCCPucG/6PL3uWT3T335N4DLppTaZN9YkzebgxmlJ0r+vL/+S9hkYl7A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Cj8Q+mDYZpMOcEe6F137SuDb0w47Gm/ypEaxL6GeAppwrhvJTVIL5gx4iFEvsyFSyoqCtqHiS1tnQsmJ2VcIDQ==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8354429973306837193">Christopher Greyson is a Wall Street Journal bestselling author of mystery, action, and thriller novels. His acclaimed Detective Jack Stratton Series has been read by over a million readers and counting. This action-packed series has a broad appeal, finding favor with mystery, thriller, and romance readers alike. The series includes <i>And Then She Was Gone, Girl Jacked, Jack Knifed, Jacks Are Wild, </i></span>
  <span id="freeText8354429973306837193" style="display:none">Christopher Greyson is a Wall Street Journal bestselling author of mystery, action, and thriller novels. His acclaimed Detective Jack Stratton Series has been read by over a million readers and counting. This action-packed series has a broad appeal, finding favor with mystery, thriller, and romance readers alike. The series includes <i>And Then She Was Gone, Girl Jacked, Jack Knifed, Jacks Are Wild, Jack and the Giant Killer, Data Jack, Jack of Hearts, Jack Frost</i>, with <i>Jack of Diamonds</i> to come. Christopher Greyson has also penned the bestselling psychological thriller, <i>The Girl Who Lived</i>, a young adult fantasy, <i>Pure of Heart</i>, and a special collection of mysteries, <i>The Adventures of Finn and Annie</i>. <br /><br />Greyson's love of mystery and adventure began with his grandfather, a World War I decorated hero. He will never forget being introduced to his grandfather's friend, a WWI pilot who flew across the skies at the same time as the feared legendary Red Baron. Since he was a little boy, Christopher Greyson dreamt of what mystery was around the next corner, or quest lay over the hill. If he couldn't find an adventure, one usually found him! Now he weaves those tales into his stories. <br /><br />Christopher Greyson's educational background is an eclectic mix of degrees in Computer Science, Theatre and Communications. He resides in Massachusetts with his lovely wife, Katherine Greyson, author of the bestselling romance-mystery series <i>Everyone Keeps Secrets</i> and their two wonderful children, Laura and Christopher. <br /><br />Christopher Greyson enjoys hearing from his readers. Please visit ChristopherGreyson.com, where you can become a preferred reader and enjoy additional FREE <i>Adventures of Finn and Annie</i>, advanced notifications of book releases and enter the giveaways and win prizes like a HD Kindle Fire Tablet! Follow Detective Jack Stratton on Twitter @chris_greyson and Facebook <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/ChristopherGreysonAuthor">https://www.facebook.com/ChristopherG...</a>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8354429973306837193" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/58107991-the-girl-who-lived">Quotes from The Girl Who Lived</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;One more question.” Henry waited until Faith put her finger down before continuing. “Do you ever remember your father wearing a baseball hat?” Like a kid flipping through the pages of a scrapbook, she ran through images of her father in her mind. No baseball cap. But it didn’t matter. Faith just wanted to stop seeing the man the world believed killed her sister. Yet the tighter she closed her eyes, the faster the images came. Her father at her horse show, sitting in the stands at Kim’s soccer game, his smiling face as he pushed her on the swing . . . Faith pressed her palms against the sides of her head and started screaming. The office door flew open. Dr. Rodgers, Titus, and two men in navy-blue suits rushed into the room. Like a boxer against the ropes, the images rained down on Faith like blows, but she was helpless to stop them. Each one sent her head reeling until she felt like she was falling—tumbling into oblivion, welcoming the darkness and an end to the pain. She felt Titus’s strong arms around her, carrying her back to her room.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/10029306-one-more-question-henry-waited-until-faith-put-her-finger">1 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;If he hadn’t been so occupied, he might have marveled at how the brain can delegate thousands of tiny mechanical motions to the body while it amuses itself by churning out an incessant silent soundtrack.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/10422272-if-he-hadn-t-been-so-occupied-he-might-have-marveled">0 likes</a>
            </nobr>
